## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Solid Mechanics / Constitutive Modeling
**Analysis**: This task belongs to solid mechanics and materials science, specifically constitutive modeling of thermomechanical behavior. It describes how stress responds to mechanical strain while accounting for temperature-induced changes in material stiffness, yield strength, and plastic flow.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime at low deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood relation: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition and strain hardening)
- Power-law plasticity: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (nonlinear plastic flow stress dependence)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturation of dislocation density with strain)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * T) (temperature-modulated stiffness and yield)
- Polynomial thermo-mechanical: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (quadratic strain hardening with thermal coefficient scaling)
- Thermal activation model: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (thermally shifted yield combined with hardening)
- Coupled logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) * (c3 + c4 * T) (low-strain nonlinearity with thermal scaling)
- Thermal expansion stress: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress from constrained thermal strain offset)
- Exponential thermal coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law strain dependence with exponential thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic response → Direct proportionality sigma ~ c * epsilon at low deformation
- Strain hardening → Power-law sigma ~ c * epsilon**n or exponential saturation with increasing epsilon
- Thermal softening of modulus/yield → Multiplicative temperature factor like (c + c * T) or exp(c * T) reducing stress magnitude
- Elastic-plastic yield point → Sudden change in slope modeled by smooth transitions or piecewise linear combinations
- Additive thermal expansion → Linear offset structure sigma ~ c * (epsilon - c * T) representing constrained thermal strain
- Dislocation multiplication → Logarithmic dependence log(1 + c * epsilon) capturing non-linear plastic flow
- Temperature-dependent phase transition → Sigmoidal or steep exponential change in material coefficients across critical T
- Coupled thermo-mechanical scaling → Separable product form f(epsilon) * g(T) where both functions scale the baseline response

  where A, B, C are constants.

  `A * epsilon**2 + B * epsilon * (T**2 - 2*C*T + C**2)`
  `= A * epsilon**2 + B * epsilon * T**2 - 2*B*C * epsilon * T + B*C**2 * epsilon`

- So GT = `c0*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon*T**2 - 2*c2*c3*epsilon*T + c2*c3**2*epsilon`.
- This is a polynomial in `epsilon` and `T`.

Wait, look at Candidate 18 again.
`epsilon*(c0 + (c1*epsilon + 1)*(T*c2*epsilon**2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**2))/(c1*epsilon + 1)`
What if `c1` is not 0? It's a rational function. GT is polynomial. Rational functions can only equal polynomials if the denominator divides the numerator exactly.
Denominator: `c1*epsilon + 1`.
Numerator: `epsilon*c0 + epsilon*(c1*epsilon+1)*(T*c2*epsilon**2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**2)`.
The second term is divisible by `c1*epsilon+1`. The first term `epsilon*c0` is not divisible by `c1*epsilon+1` unless `c0=0`.
If `c0=0`, it simplifies to `epsilon*(T*c2*epsilon**2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**2) = c2*T*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**3`. Cubic.
So 18 is `[NO MATCH]`.

Let's check Candidate 26 again.
Denominator `c2+epsilon`. Numerator `T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+epsilon)*(c3+epsilon)**2 + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6`.
For it to be polynomial, `c2+epsilon` must divide `T*c0 + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6`.
This requires `c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + (c6 + T*c0)` to be divisible by `epsilon + c2`.
By polynomial division, remainder is `c4*(-c2)**2 + c5*(-c2) + c6 + T*c0 = c4*c2**2 - c5*c2 + c6 + T*c0`.
For this to be 0 for all T, we need `c0=0` and `c4*c2**2 - c5*c2 + c6 = 0`.
If `c0=0`, the expression becomes `T*c1*(c3+epsilon)**2 + (c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6)/(c2+epsilon)`.
The second part is a constant or linear in epsilon.
So it becomes `T*c1*(c3**2 + 2*c3*epsilon + epsilon**2) + A*epsilon + B`.
`= T*c1*c3**2 + 2*T*c1*c3*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + A*epsilon + B`.
Terms: `T`, `T*epsilon`, `T*epsilon**2`, `epsilon`, constant.
GT has `epsilon**2`, `epsilon*T**2`, `epsilon*T`, `epsilon`.
Mismatch.

Let's check Candidate 33 again.
